{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01CwTxyT4Jj1roQZqeM3dcCn","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01KNzXP7Jw9wmRHiDbXQ3KYc","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubernetes API Server Library: Architecture and Extension Guide\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes apiserver library (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver`) is the core request processing framework that powers Kubernetes API servers. It provides a modular, composable architecture for handling HTTP requests, authenticating users, authorizing actions, validating and mutating objects, and persisting data. This document explains the subsystem's architecture, end-to-end request flows, and extension mechanisms from the perspective of operators and developers who need to understand or customize the system.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe apiserver library implements the complete request handling pipeline for a Kubernetes-compatible API server. Its primary responsibilities are:\n\n- **Request Routing**: Dispatch incoming HTTP requests to appropriate handlers based on URL patterns and API resource metadata\n- **Request Processing Pipeline**: Chain filters that handle cross-cutting concerns (authentication, authorization, audit, admission control)\n- **API Resource Management**: Register and expose API groups, versions, and resources through a discovery mechanism\n- **Object Storage Abstraction**: Provide a unified interface to persistent storage backends (etcd) with support for serialization, versioning, and transformations\n- **Request Context Enrichment**: Attach authentication/authorization information, metadata, and trace context to requests flowing through the system\n- **Response Handling**: Serialize objects according to negotiated content types and handle errors consistently\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**What the apiserver library handles:**\n- HTTP request/response plumbing\n- Authentication and authorization enforcement\n- Admission control (validation and mutation)\n- Audit logging\n- OpenAPI/Swagger documentation generation\n- Storage interface for CRUD operations\n- Common error handling and response formatting\n\n**What it delegates:**\n- **Authentication mechanism implementation**: Delegated to pluggable authenticators (clients must provide `authenticator.Authenticator`)\n- **Authorization decision logic**: Delegated to pluggable authorizers (clients must provide `authorizer.Authorizer`)\n- **Persistent storage backend**: Delegated to storage implementations (etcd3, testing backends)\n- **Admission plugin implementation**: Delegated to admission controllers (clients implement `admission.MutationInterface` or `admission.ValidationInterface`)\n- **Resource business logic**: Delegated to REST storage handlers\n- **Binary startup and configuration**: Delegated to consuming binaries (kube-apiserver, custom API servers)\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\nThe apiserver library depends on:\n- **k8s.io/apimachinery**: Core runtime, serialization, object marshaling/unmarshaling\n- **k8s.io/client-go**: For loopback client configuration and informers\n- **k8s.io/component-base**: Shared components like logging, metrics, feature gates, tracing\n- **go-restful**: HTTP routing and web service registration\n- **etcd client libraries**: For storage backend interaction\n- **kube-openapi**: OpenAPI schema and documentation generation\n\n### Downstream Dependents\n\nThe library is consumed by:\n- **kube-apiserver**: Main Kubernetes API server\n- **aggregation-apiserver**: API server for aggregated APIs\n- **Custom API servers**: User-built servers using the library (sample-apiserver, etc.)\n- **apiextensions-apiserver**: Handles CustomResourceDefinitions\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Division\n\n### 2.1 Server Core (`pkg/server/`)\n\n**GenericAPIServer** (`genericapiserver.go`): The central orchestrator that manages the complete server lifecycle.\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Holds server configuration (authentication, authorization, admission, storage)\n- Manages the HTTP handler chain and handler director\n- Coordinates API group installation\n- Manages lifecycle hooks (PreStartHooks, PostStartHooks)\n- Coordinates graceful shutdown\n- Tracks health status (healthz, livez, readyz checks)\n\n**Config** (`config.go`): The comprehensive configuration struct that accumulates all settings needed to construct a working API server.\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Captures authentication/authorization configuration\n- Stores admission control, audit backend, and storage transformers\n- Contains request/response tuning parameters (timeouts, body size limits, in-flight limits)\n- Defines the handler chain builder function\n- Stores feature gates, serializers, and OpenAPI configuration\n\n**APIServerHandler** (`handler.go`): Routes incoming requests to appropriate handlers.\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Maintains GoRestful container for REST API registration\n- Maintains NonGoRestfulMux for non-standard endpoints\n- Implements director pattern to intelligently route requests\n- Falls through to appropriate handler based on registered web services\n\n### 2.2 Request Filtering Pipeline (`pkg/server/filters/`, `pkg/endpoints/filters/`)\n\nThe handler chain applies a series of filters that process requests before they reach API handlers. Filters are applied **in order**, and each wraps the next:\n\n**Critical Filters (in application order):**\n1. **AuditInit** (`filters/audit_init.go`): Initialize audit logging context\n2. **PanicRecovery** (`filters/panic_recovery.go`): Recover from panics and prevent crashes\n3. **RequestInfo** (`filters/request_info.go`): Parse URL and attach RequestInfo to context (resource, verb, namespace, etc.)\n4. **MuxAndDiscoveryComplete** (`filters/mux_discovery_complete.go`): Signal when mux is ready\n5. **RequestReceivedTimestamp** (`filters/request_received_time.go`): Mark when request was received\n6. **HTTPLogging** (`filters/http_logging.go`): Log HTTP requests at debug level\n7. **LatencyTrackers** (`filters/latency_tracker.go`): Track filter execution latencies\n8. **ProbabilisticGoaway** (HTTP/2): Send periodic GOAWAY to rebalance load\n9. **HSTS** (`filters/hsts.go`): Add HSTS security headers\n10. **RetryAfter** (`filters/retry_after.go`): Signal shutdown via Retry-After header\n11. **CacheControl** (`filters/cachecontrol.go`): Add cache control headers\n12. **TimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests** (`filters/timeout.go`): Apply request timeout\n13. **RequestDeadline** (`filters/request_deadline.go`): Track and enforce request deadline\n14. **WaitGroup** (`filters/wait_group.go`): Track request completion for shutdown\n15. **WatchTerminationDuringShutdown** (`filters/watch_termination.go`): Handle watch during shutdown\n16. **Authentication** (`filters/authentication.go`): Validate user credentials; on failure, invoke unauthorized handler\n17. **Audit** (`filters/audit.go`): Log request/response for audit trail\n18. **Impersonation** (`filters/impersonation/`): Handle user/group impersonation\n19. **PriorityAndFairness** (`server/filters/`): Apply flow control and priority/fairness queuing\n20. **Authorization** (`filters/authorization.go`): Verify user has permission for action\n\nEach filter can examine/modify the request and context, and can short-circuit by directly writing a response (e.g., auth failure).\n\n### 2.3 Endpoint Installation and Handler Registration (`pkg/endpoints/`)\n\n**APIInstaller** (`installer.go`): Registers API resource handlers into the GoRestful container.\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Introspects REST storage objects to discover verbs (GET, POST, PUT, PATCH, DELETE, WATCH)\n- Creates gorestful routes for each verb\n- Constructs RequestScope with serialization, validation, and storage configuration\n- Associates handlers (get, create, update, delete, watch, patch, etc.) with routes\n- Generates OpenAPI documentation for discovered resources\n\n**APIGroupVersion** (`groupversion.go`): Represents a single API group version (e.g., \"apps/v1\").\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Holds VersionedResourcesStorageMap mapping resource names to REST storage implementations\n- Provides REST storage interfaces for each resource\n- Collaborates with APIInstaller to expose resources as HTTP endpoints\n\n### 2.4 Request Handlers (`pkg/endpoints/handlers/`)\n\nThese handlers implement CRUD operations on resources. Each handler operates within a **RequestScope** which provides:\n- Serializer: For encoding/decoding objects\n- Storage: The backend REST storage\n- Authorizer: For authorization checks\n- Admission: For validation/mutation\n- FieldManager: For server-side apply and managed fields tracking\n\n**Key Handlers:**\n- **create.go** (`CreateResource`): Handle POST requests; calls admission, then storage.Create\n- **get.go** (`GetResource`): Handle GET requests; calls storage.Get, applies authorization checks\n- **list.go** (via rest.go): Handle LIST requests; applies filtering, pagination\n- **update.go** (`UpdateResource`): Handle PUT requests; validates, mutates, then storage.Update\n- **patch.go** (`PatchResource`): Handle PATCH requests; applies JSONPatch or strategic merge patch, then storage.Update\n- **delete.go** (`DeleteResource`): Handle DELETE requests; calls storage.Delete with cascading delete strategy\n- **watch.go** (`WatchResource`): Handle WATCH requests; streams server-sent updates from storage\n\n**Shared Responsibility Pattern:**\nEach handler follows this pattern:\n1. Decode the incoming request body\n2. Apply defaults (if applicable)\n3. Run **mutating admission** (allows modification)\n4. Validate the object\n5. Run **validating admission** (no modification allowed)\n6. Call **storage** interface\n7. Encode and write response\n\n### 2.5 Admission Control (`pkg/admission/`)\n\nAdmission control is a two-phase system that allows pluggable policies to validate and mutate requests:\n\n**Interfaces:**\n- **MutationInterface** (`interfaces.go`): Can examine and modify objects\n- **ValidationInterface** (`interfaces.go`): Can only validate; no mutations allowed\n\n**Phases:**\n1. **Mutating Admission** (before validation): Plugins can modify the object (e.g., DefaultServiceAccount, LimitRanger)\n2. **Validating Admission** (after mutation): Plugins validate the final object (e.g., ResourceQuota, PodSecurityPolicy)\n\n**Attributes Interface** (`attributes.go`): Provides request context to admission plugins:\n- Operation (CREATE, UPDATE, DELETE, CONNECT)\n- Resource identity (namespace, name, resource, kind)\n- User information\n- Object and old object\n- Dry-run flag\n- Annotations capability (allows plugins to leave notes on the audit trail)\n\n**Chain** (`chain.go`): Chains multiple admission plugins into a single interface; short-circuits on first error.\n\n### 2.6 Authentication and Authorization\n\n**Authentication** (`pkg/authentication/`):\n- **Authenticator interface**: Examines request and produces `user.Info` containing username, uid, groups, and extra attributes\n- **Multiple authenticator chains** can be composed (union authenticator)\n- Pluggable implementations: X.509 certificates, bearer tokens, basic auth, service account tokens, OIDC, etc.\n\n**Authorization** (`pkg/authorization/`):\n- **Authorizer interface**: Examines request + user and returns Allow/Deny/NoOpinion\n- **Pluggable implementations**: RBAC (role-based), ABAC (attribute-based), webhook, node authorization, etc.\n- **RuleResolver** interface: Lists which rules/roles apply to a user in a namespace (used for discovery)\n\n### 2.7 Storage (`pkg/storage/`)\n\n**Storage Interfaces** (`storage/interfaces.go`):\n- **Interface** (base): New(), Destroy() methods\n- **Getter**: Get(ctx, key) → object\n- **Lister**: List(ctx, opts) → objects\n- **Creator**: Create(ctx, key, obj, ttl) → object\n- **Updater**: Update(ctx, key, obj, fn) → object\n- **Deleter**: Delete(ctx, key, obj) → deleted object\n- **Watcher**: Watch(ctx, opts) → events channel\n\n**Storage Backend** (`etcd3/`): Implements the interfaces using etcd3 as persistent storage.\n\n**Cacher** (`cacher/`): Wraps storage with in-memory list/watch caching for performance.\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- CRUD operations on versioned objects\n- Watch streaming (sends updates as objects change)\n- Atomic conditional updates (CAS)\n- TTL/deletion grace periods\n- Encryption transformers (for secrets)\n- Resource version tracking\n\n### 2.8 Request Context (`pkg/endpoints/request/`)\n\nThe request context carries information through the pipeline:\n\n**RequestInfo** (`requestinfo.go`): Parsed from URL; contains:\n- Verb (get, list, create, update, delete, watch, patch, proxy, connect)\n- Resource, subresource, name, namespace\n- IsResourceRequest (distinguishes API resource requests from system endpoints)\n\n**Request Context Keys** (`context.go`):\n- User information (set by authentication filter)\n- Namespace (set by RequestInfo filter)\n\n**Decorators** that can be attached to context:\n- ReceivedTime: When request arrived at server\n- RequestDeadline: Deadline for request execution\n- WebhookDuration: Time spent in webhooks\n\n### 2.9 Discovery and OpenAPI (`pkg/endpoints/discovery/`)\n\n**Discovery Handlers** (`discovery/`):\n- **Root discovery** (`discovery/root.go`): Lists API groups at `/apis`\n- **Group version discovery** (`discovery/group.go`): Lists resources in a version at `/apis/group/v1`\n- **Legacy discovery** (`discovery/legacy.go`): Lists core API v1 resources\n- **Aggregated discovery** (`discovery/aggregated/`): Efficient discovery via gzip and ETags\n\n**OpenAPI** (`endpoints/openapi.go`):\n- Generates OpenAPI v2 spec from registered resources\n- Generates OpenAPI v3 spec\n- Exposes at `/openapi/v2`, `/openapi/v3`\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow with Evidence\n\n### Example: Creating a Pod\n\nThis traces a real request through the system with file references.\n\n**HTTP Request:**\n```\nPOST /api/v1/namespaces/default/pods HTTP/1.1\nContent-Type: application/json\nAuthorization: Bearer <token>\n\n{\"apiVersion\": \"v1\", \"kind\": \"Pod\", ...}\n```\n\n### Step-by-Step Flow\n\n#### Phase 1: Handler Chain Filters\n\n**1. Request arrives at `APIServerHandler.FullHandlerChain`** → `handler.go:95`\n   - The FullHandlerChain wraps all filters around the Director\n\n**2. AuditInit** → `filters/audit_init.go:23`\n   ```go\n   func WithAuditInit(handler http.Handler) http.Handler {\n       // Initialize audit context with zero values\n   }\n   ```\n   - Creates empty audit event structure\n   - Allows subsequent filters/handlers to populate audit details\n\n**3. PanicRecovery** → `filters/panic_recovery.go`\n   ```go\n   func WithPanicRecovery(handler http.Handler, ...) http.Handler {\n       // Recovers from panics in handler chain\n   }\n   ```\n\n**4. RequestInfo** → `filters/requestinfo.go:32`\n   ```go\n   func WithRequestInfo(handler http.Handler, resolver RequestInfoResolver) http.Handler {\n       // Parse request path to extract:\n       // - Verb: \"create\"\n       // - Resource: \"pods\"\n       // - Namespace: \"default\"\n       // - APIVersion: \"v1\"\n   }\n   ```\n   - Calls `RequestInfoResolver` to parse URL path\n   - Attaches RequestInfo to request context (`request.WithValue(ctx, requestInfoKey, info)`)\n\n**5. HTTPLogging** → `filters/http_logging.go`\n   - Logs request at debug level\n\n**6. LatencyTrackers** → `filters/latency_tracker.go`\n   - Tracks filter execution duration\n\n**7-11. Security and Infrastructure Filters**\n   - HSTS headers, cache control, timeout enforcement, wait group tracking\n\n**12. TimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests** → `server/filters/timeout.go`\n   ```go\n   func WithTimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests(handler http.Handler, ...) http.Handler {\n       // Check LongRunningFunc (returns false for Pod creation)\n       // If not long-running, wrap handler in goroutine with timeout context\n   }\n   ```\n\n**13. Authentication** → `filters/authentication.go:60`\n   ```go\n   func WithAuthentication(handler http.Handler, auth Authenticator, ...) http.Handler {\n       // Call authenticator with request\n       // Extract bearer token from Authorization header\n       // Validate JWT/certificate/etc.\n       // Set user in context: request.WithUser(ctx, userInfo)\n   }\n   ```\n   - Extracts bearer token from Authorization header\n   - Calls pluggable authenticator (e.g., JWT validator, certificate validator)\n   - On success: attaches `user.Info` to context\n   - On failure: immediately responds with 401 Unauthorized (invokes failedHandler)\n\n**14. Impersonation** → `filters/impersonation/impersonation.go:102`\n   ```go\n   func (handler impersonationHandler) ServeHTTP(w http.ResponseWriter, req *http.Request) {\n       // If \"Impersonate-User\" header is set and user is authorized to impersonate:\n       // Replace user in context with target user\n       // Check user.RbacApiVersion to validate authorization\n   }\n   ```\n   - Allows privileged users to impersonate others\n   - Checks impersonate-* headers\n   - Validates authorization for impersonation action\n\n**15. Audit** → `filters/audit.go:80`\n   ```go\n   func WithAudit(handler http.Handler, backend Backend, ...) http.Handler {\n       // Determine if request should be audited (via policy)\n       // Wrap response writer to capture response\n       // Log audit event after response\n   }\n   ```\n   - Evaluates audit policy to determine audit level (None, Metadata, RequestResponse)\n   - Wraps response writer to capture response data\n   - Will log request/response to audit backend after handler completes\n\n**16. PriorityAndFairness** → `server/filters/priorityandfairness.go`\n   ```go\n   func WithPriorityAndFairness(handler http.Handler, ...) http.Handler {\n       // Check if flow control is enabled\n       // Estimate request work (read/write cost)\n       // Acquire seat in priority/fairness queue\n       // If queue full, respond 429 Too Many Requests\n   }\n   ```\n   - Implements fine-grained priority and fairness for request handling\n   - Queues requests if system is overloaded\n   - Responds 429 if request cannot be admitted\n\n**17. Authorization** → `filters/authorization.go:50`\n   ```go\n   func WithAuthorization(handler http.Handler, auth Authorizer, ...) http.Handler {\n       // Call authorizer with request attributes\n       // Check if user is allowed to perform action\n       // Decision: Allow/Deny/NoOpinion\n   }\n   ```\n   - Creates authorization attributes (verb, resource, namespace, etc.) from RequestInfo\n   - Calls pluggable authorizer (e.g., RBAC evaluator)\n   - On Deny: responds 403 Forbidden\n   - On Allow: continues to API handler\n\n#### Phase 2: Director Routes to Handler\n\n**18. Director** → `handler.go:121`\n   ```go\n   func (d director) ServeHTTP(w http.ResponseWriter, req *http.Request) {\n       // For /api/v1/..., check if GoRestful has a registered service\n       // If yes, route to GoRestfulContainer\n       // If no, route to NonGoRestfulMux\n   }\n   ```\n   - Checks registered gorestful web services\n   - Path `/api/v1/namespaces/...` matches the core API v1 service\n   - Routes to `GoRestfulContainer.Dispatch()`\n\n#### Phase 3: API Handler\n\n**19. GoRestful routing** → Via `go-restful` library\n   - Matches route `/api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/pods` against registered routes\n   - Extracts path parameters (namespace = \"default\")\n   - Invokes registered handler function\n\n**20. Create Handler** → `handlers/create.go:40`\n   ```go\n   func (h *createHandler) Create(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {\n       // 1. Decode request body\n       obj, gvk, err := scope.Decoder.Decode(r.Body, nil, nil)\n\n       // 2. Apply defaults\n       scope.Defaulter.Default(obj)\n\n       // 3. Mutating admission\n       if err := h.admission.Admit(ctx, attr, scope); err != nil {\n           scope.err(err, w, r)\n           return\n       }\n\n       // 4. Validate\n       if errs := validation.ValidatePod(obj); errs != nil {\n           scope.err(errs.ToAggregate(), w, r)\n           return\n       }\n\n       // 5. Validating admission\n       if err := h.admission.Validate(ctx, attr, scope); err != nil {\n           scope.err(err, w, r)\n           return\n       }\n\n       // 6. Storage create\n       out, err := h.storage.Create(ctx, key, obj, ttl)\n\n       // 7. Write response\n       responsewriters.WriteObject(w, obj, scope)\n   }\n   ```\n\n   **Substeps in detail:**\n\n   **20a. Decode Request Body** → `handlers/rest.go:150`\n   - Negotiation handler determines content type (JSON, YAML, Protobuf)\n   - Uses `scope.Serializer` to decode bytes into runtime.Object\n\n   **20b. Set Defaults** → Via `runtime.ObjectDefaulter`\n   - Applied before admission so admission sees defaults\n\n   **20c. Mutating Admission Phase** → `admission/chain.go:25`\n   - Iterates through plugins implementing MutationInterface\n   - Each plugin can modify object (e.g., inject service account)\n   - Creates `admission.Attributes` from request context and RequestInfo\n   - Short-circuits on first error\n\n   **20d. Validation**\n   - Calls built-in validation rules (e.g., `validation.ValidatePod`)\n   - Returns aggregated errors if any field is invalid\n\n   **20e. Validating Admission Phase** → `admission/chain.go:40`\n   - Iterates through plugins implementing ValidationInterface\n   - Can only reject, not modify\n   - Checks final state after mutations\n\n   **20f. Storage Create** → `handlers/create.go:75`\n   ```go\n   key := computeKey(namespace, name)  // \"pods/default/pod-name\"\n   out, err := storage.Create(ctx, key, obj, options.TTL)\n   ```\n   - Calls underlying storage (etcd3, test backend, etc.)\n   - Key is computed from namespace + name\n   - Storage returns versioned object with `metadata.resourceVersion` set\n   - Storage triggers watch event notifications\n\n   **20g. Write Response** → `handlers/response.go:35`\n   ```go\n   func WriteObject(w http.ResponseWriter, obj runtime.Object, scope *RequestScope) {\n       // 1. Negotiate serialization format from Accept header\n       // 2. Encode object using negotiated serializer\n       // 3. Write HTTP 201 Created response\n       // 4. Include Location header with resource URL\n       // 5. Include Content-Type header\n   }\n   ```\n\n#### Phase 4: Audit Logging (After Response)\n\n**21. Audit Backend** → `filters/audit.go:95`\n   - Previously wrapped response writer during audit filter\n   - Now that response is complete, logs audit event:\n   ```\n   {\n     \"verb\": \"create\",\n     \"user\": {\"username\": \"alice@example.com\", \"groups\": [\"developers\"]},\n     \"sourceIPs\": [\"10.0.0.5\"],\n     \"objectRef\": {\"resource\": \"pods\", \"namespace\": \"default\", \"name\": \"my-pod\"},\n     \"requestObject\": {...pod...},\n     \"responseStatus\": {\"code\": 201},\n     \"responseObject\": {...pod...},\n     \"stage\": \"ResponseComplete\"\n   }\n   ```\n\n#### Phase 5: Storage Triggers Watch Events\n\n**22. Storage Watch Notification** → `storage/etcd3/store.go`\n   - Any active watch clients receive the update event\n   - Event contains object, operation (Added), and resource version\n\n### Request Flow Diagram\n\n```\nHTTP Request\n    ↓\nAuditInit → PanicRecovery → RequestInfo → ... → Authentication\n    ↓\nUser identified and attached to context\n    ↓\nImpersonation → Audit (wraps response) → PriorityAndFairness → Authorization\n    ↓\nAuthorization approved\n    ↓\nDirector Router\n    ↓\nGoRestful → API Handler (CreateHandler)\n    ↓\nDecode → Defaults → MutatingAdmission → Validate → ValidatingAdmission → Storage.Create\n    ↓\nResponse written (201 Created)\n    ↓\nWatch events notified\n    ↓\nAudit event logged\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n#### Authentication Failure\n- **Symptom**: 401 Unauthorized response\n- **Root causes**: Invalid token, expired certificate, unknown authenticator\n- **Impact**: User cannot access API\n- **Recovery**: User obtains new credentials\n- **Design choice**: Fail-closed for security; no request proceeds without authentication\n\n#### Authorization Failure\n- **Symptom**: 403 Forbidden response\n- **Root causes**: RBAC rule doesn't permit action, webhook denies request\n- **Impact**: User cannot perform action\n- **Recovery**: Admin updates RBAC rules\n- **Design choice**: Fails fast before admission plugins run; prevents wasted work\n\n#### Admission Webhook Timeout\n- **Symptom**: Request eventually fails (default 30s timeout); webhook never responds\n- **Root causes**: Webhook server crash, network partition, slow webhook\n- **Impact**: Request is rejected and user receives 500 error\n- **Recovery**: Fix webhook, retry request\n- **Design choice**: Webhooks have timeouts to prevent unbounded request latency\n- **Evidence**: `handlers/create.go:95` - admission is called within request timeout\n\n#### Storage Failure (etcd unavailable)\n- **Symptom**: 500 Internal Server Error response; readiness check fails\n- **Root causes**: etcd cluster down, network partition, disk full\n- **Impact**: Cannot persist data; all mutations fail\n- **Recovery**: Restore etcd cluster\n- **Mitigations**: Caching layer provides read availability; watch buffering masks brief outages\n- **Evidence**: `storage/cacher/cacher.go` - cacher wraps storage for high availability\n\n#### Request Timeout\n- **Symptom**: Request context exceeds deadline; connection reset\n- **Root causes**: Long-running operation, slow storage, overloaded system\n- **Impact**: Client receives error or connection closes\n- **Recovery**: Automatic retry (if client implements it)\n- **Design choice**: Non-long-running requests get strict timeout; long-running (watch) get graceful timeout\n- **Evidence**: `config.go:228` - RequestTimeout parameter; `filters/timeout.go` - timeout enforcement\n\n#### Flow Control Rejection\n- **Symptom**: 429 Too Many Requests response\n- **Root causes**: Request queue full, priority level saturated\n- **Impact**: Client must retry with backoff\n- **Recovery**: Automatic retry by client\n- **Design choice**: Protects system from overload; fair queuing prevents thundering herd\n- **Evidence**: `config.go:254-259` - flow control configuration; `server/filters/priorityandfairness.go`\n\n#### Panic in Handler\n- **Symptom**: 500 Internal Server Error response\n- **Root causes**: Bug in handler code, admission plugin, storage, or business logic\n- **Impact**: Request fails but server continues running\n- **Recovery**: Fix bug, redeploy\n- **Design choice**: Panic recovery prevents cascading failures\n- **Evidence**: `filters/panic_recovery.go` - wraps handler chain\n\n### 4.2 Design Limits\n\n#### MaxRequestBodyBytes\n- **Parameter**: `config.go:253`\n- **Default**: Typically 1.5MB for kube-apiserver\n- **Purpose**: Prevent unbounded memory usage from large request bodies\n- **Impact**: Large objects (e.g., big ConfigMaps) can hit this limit\n- **Mitigation**: Clients can split large objects; etcd has its own 1.5GB limit\n\n#### MaxRequestsInFlight / MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight\n- **Parameters**: `config.go:256-259`\n- **Default**: 200 read, 100 write for kube-apiserver\n- **Purpose**: Bound concurrency to prevent resource exhaustion\n- **Impact**: Beyond limit, requests queue and receive 429 if queue full\n- **Modern alternative**: Priority and Fairness (`config.go:140`) is more sophisticated\n\n#### RequestTimeout / MinRequestTimeout\n- **Parameters**: `config.go:228-231`\n- **Default**: 1 minute read, 1 hour watch\n- **Purpose**: Prevent unbounded connections\n- **Tradeoff**: Too short and legitimate operations fail; too long and broken clients hold connections\n- **Evidence**: `filters/timeout.go` - timeout is applied per RequestScope\n\n#### Storage Watch Buffer\n- **Location**: `storage/cacher/cacher.go`\n- **Default**: Small bounded buffer for watch events\n- **Purpose**: Decouple event production from consumption\n- **Tradeoff**: Clients watching many objects can fall behind; buffer overflow causes watch restart\n\n### 4.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### GoRestful vs. Custom Routing\n- **Choice**: Uses go-restful library for REST endpoint registration\n- **Advantages**: Structured OpenAPI documentation, parameter marshaling, content negotiation\n- **Disadvantages**: Added latency, less flexible than custom routing\n- **Alternative considered**: Custom HTTP mux\n- **Evidence**: `handler.go:73-100` - NewAPIServerHandler uses restful.Container\n\n#### Request Filtering Chain vs. Middleware\n- **Choice**: Sequential filter chain (each filter wraps next)\n- **Advantages**: Order is explicit and debuggable; filters can short-circuit (e.g., auth failure)\n- **Disadvantages**: Deeply nested function calls; filter order is critical and easy to get wrong\n- **Evidence**: `config.go:1015-1097` - DefaultBuildHandlerChain shows exact order\n\n#### Admission Webhooks in-process\n- **Choice**: Webhooks are called synchronously during request handling\n- **Advantages**: Strongly ordered; failure during mutation is clear\n- **Disadvantages**: Webhook latency directly impacts request latency; webhook crash can bring down API server\n- **Alternative considered**: Async webhook queuing\n- **Evidence**: `handlers/create.go:40-75` - admission is called before storage\n\n#### Separated Mutating and Validating Admission\n- **Choice**: Two phases (mutating first, then validating)\n- **Advantages**: Plugins can assume objects are validated before seeing them (in validate phase)\n- **Disadvantages**: Complexity; must document which phase to use\n- **Evidence**: `admission/interfaces.go:129-144` - separate interfaces\n\n#### In-Memory Cacher Wrapping Storage\n- **Choice**: Cacher is optional but on by default\n- **Advantages**: Dramatically improves list/watch performance; provides high availability during brief etcd outages\n- **Disadvantages**: Added complexity; consistency window (watch lag); memory overhead\n- **Evidence**: `storage/cacher/cacher.go:40` - cacher wraps storage.Interface\n\n#### Authentication Separate from Authorization\n- **Choice**: Authentication identifies who; authorization determines what they can do\n- **Advantages**: Clear separation of concerns; allows different auth mechanisms (cert, token, proxy header)\n- **Disadvantages**: Auth information must flow through context; two separate plugins must agree\n- **Evidence**: `filters/authentication.go`, `filters/authorization.go` - separate stages\n\n#### Audit Wrapped Around Response\n- **Choice**: Response writer is wrapped during audit filter to capture body\n- **Advantages**: Audit sees actual response sent to client\n- **Disadvantages**: Response is buffered in memory; large responses consume memory\n- **Evidence**: `filters/audit.go:80` - response is wrapped\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 5.1 Server Configuration Extension\n\n**Location**: `server/config.go` - Config struct\n\n**Extension points:**\n\n1. **BuildHandlerChainFunc** (`config.go:186`)\n   ```go\n   type Config struct {\n       BuildHandlerChainFunc func(apiHandler http.Handler, c *Config) http.Handler\n   }\n   ```\n   - **Purpose**: Allows replacing the entire filter chain\n   - **Default**: `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` (all standard filters)\n   - **Use case**: Add custom filters (e.g., tenant isolation, request deduplication)\n   - **Risk**: Incorrect filter ordering can break security; inserting in wrong place can leak auth context\n   - **Evidence**: `config.go:1015` - DefaultBuildHandlerChain shows correct order\n   - **Recommendation**: Only append filters; don't reorder standard filters\n\n2. **RequestInfoResolver** (`config.go:210`)\n   ```go\n   RequestInfoResolver apirequest.RequestInfoResolver\n   ```\n   - **Purpose**: Customizes how request URL is parsed into RequestInfo\n   - **Default**: `apirequest.DefaultRequestInfoResolver`\n   - **Use case**: Custom URL schemes (e.g., `/custom-api-version/...`)\n   - **Risk**: Wrong path parsing can cause authorization bypass (resource mismatch)\n   - **Evidence**: `filters/requestinfo.go` - uses resolver to parse path\n\n3. **Serializer** (`config.go:213`)\n   ```go\n   Serializer runtime.NegotiatedSerializer\n   ```\n   - **Purpose**: Determines how objects are encoded/decoded\n   - **Default**: Typically `api.Codecs` from client-go\n   - **Use case**: Support additional content types\n   - **Risk**: Incorrect serialization can corrupt data or cause deserialization panics\n   - **Evidence**: `handlers/rest.go:70-90` - serializer negotiation\n\n4. **Authenticator** (`config.go:117`)\n   ```go\n   type AuthenticationInfo struct {\n       Authenticator authenticator.Authenticator\n   }\n   ```\n   - **Purpose**: Determines how users are authenticated\n   - **Default**: Chain of multiple authenticators (cert, bearer token, basic auth, etc.)\n   - **Use case**: Add custom authentication (e.g., custom JWT validator, LDAP)\n   - **Risk**: Wrong authentication can grant access to unintended users; weak validators are a security vulnerability\n   - **Evidence**: `filters/authentication.go:60` - authenticator is called\n\n5. **Authorizer** (`config.go:120`)\n   ```go\n   type AuthorizationInfo struct {\n       Authorizer authorizer.Authorizer\n   }\n   ```\n   - **Purpose**: Determines what actions are allowed\n   - **Default**: RBAC authorizer + delegating authorizer for webhooks\n   - **Use case**: Add custom authorization (e.g., attribute-based, geo-aware, time-based)\n   - **Risk**: Overly permissive authorizer grants unintended access; overly restrictive breaks legitimate operations\n   - **Evidence**: `filters/authorization.go:50` - authorizer is called\n\n6. **AdmissionControl** (`config.go:136`)\n   ```go\n   AdmissionControl admission.Interface\n   ```\n   - **Purpose**: Validates and mutates requests\n   - **Default**: Chain of admission plugins (ResourceQuota, PodSecurityPolicy, etc.)\n   - **Use case**: Custom validation rules, automatic object mutation (e.g., inject sidecar)\n   - **Risk**: Admission can modify or reject user requests; malicious plugins can corrupt data or cause denials of service\n   - **Evidence**: `handlers/create.go:45-50` - admission runs before storage\n\n7. **FlowControl** (`config.go:140`)\n   ```go\n   FlowControl utilflowcontrol.Interface\n   ```\n   - **Purpose**: Implements priority and fairness for request handling\n   - **Default**: Priority and Fairness feature (if enabled); fallback to simple in-flight limits\n   - **Use case**: Custom queuing, priority level definitions\n   - **Risk**: Incorrect priority levels can cause starvation of legitimate traffic\n   - **Evidence**: `server/filters/priorityandfairness.go`\n\n8. **AuditBackend** (`config.go:171`)\n   ```go\n   AuditBackend audit.Backend\n   ```\n   - **Purpose**: Where audit events are written\n   - **Default**: File backend or webhook backend\n   - **Use case**: Send audit events to custom logging system (Splunk, Datadog, CloudWatch)\n   - **Risk**: Audit backend failure can cause request failures if not handled gracefully\n   - **Evidence**: `filters/audit.go:80` - backend is called after response\n\n### 5.2 Admission Control Extension\n\n**Location**: `pkg/admission/`\n\n**How to implement a custom admission plugin:**\n\n1. **Implement MutationInterface** (if mutations are allowed):\n   ```go\n   type MyPlugin struct{}\n\n   func (p *MyPlugin) Admit(ctx context.Context, a admission.Attributes, o admission.ObjectInterfaces) error {\n       // Examine request in attributes\n       // Modify object if needed\n       // Return error to reject\n   }\n\n   func (p *MyPlugin) Handles(operation admission.Operation) bool {\n       return operation == admission.Create // Only for creates\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Implement ValidationInterface** (if only validation):\n   ```go\n   func (p *MyPlugin) Validate(ctx context.Context, a admission.Attributes, o admission.ObjectInterfaces) error {\n       // Check object state\n       // Return error to reject (cannot modify)\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Register plugin** in the admission chain (at binary startup)\n\n**Attributes available to plugins** (`admission/attributes.go`):\n- GetName(), GetNamespace(), GetResource(), GetSubresource()\n- GetOperation() (CREATE, UPDATE, DELETE, CONNECT)\n- GetObject(), GetOldObject() (for UPDATE and DELETE)\n- GetUserInfo() (user making request)\n- IsDryRun() (is this a dry-run?)\n- AddAnnotation() (add audit annotations)\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Performance**: Slow plugins block all requests\n- **Correctness**: Buggy plugins can corrupt data or cause indefinite loops\n- **Security**: Plugins have access to full object including secrets\n- **Cascading failures**: Webhook plugins that crash can bring down API server\n\n**Evidence**: `handlers/create.go:45-75` - admission is called synchronously\n\n### 5.3 Storage Backend Extension\n\n**Location**: `pkg/storage/interfaces.go`\n\n**Storage interface**:\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    Create(ctx context.Context, key string, obj runtime.Object, ttl uint64) (runtime.Object, error)\n    Get(ctx context.Context, key string, opts GetOptions) (runtime.Object, error)\n    List(ctx context.Context, key string, opts ListOptions) (runtime.ObjectList, error)\n    Update(ctx context.Context, key string, obj runtime.Object, ...) (runtime.Object, error)\n    Delete(ctx context.Context, key string, opts DeleteOptions) (runtime.Object, error)\n    Watch(ctx context.Context, key string, opts ListOptions) (watch.Interface, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Custom backend example**: In-memory testing backend, MySQL backend, DynamoDB backend\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Consistency**: Backends must correctly handle versioning and conflicts\n- **Transactions**: Some operations require atomic multi-key updates (cascading delete)\n- **Performance**: Slow backends affect all API operations\n- **Data loss**: Bugs can cause data corruption or loss\n\n**Evidence**: `storage/interfaces.go` - interface definition; `storage/etcd3/store.go` - etcd3 implementation\n\n### 5.4 REST Handler and Storage Extension\n\n**Location**: `pkg/registry/rest/`\n\n**Storage interface** - minimum implementation:\n```go\ntype Storage interface {\n    New() runtime.Object\n    Destroy()\n}\n\n// Optional interfaces for advanced operations:\ntype Getter interface {\n    Get(ctx context.Context, name string, options *metav1.GetOptions) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n\ntype Creater interface {\n    Create(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object, ...) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n\ntype Updater interface {\n    Update(ctx context.Context, name string, objInfo UpdatedObjectInfo, ...) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\n**How REST handlers use storage**:\n- Request comes in → Handler looks up Storage implementation for resource\n- Handler creates `RequestScope` with storage\n- Handler calls storage method (Create, Get, Update, etc.)\n- Storage returns object with updated metadata (resourceVersion, etc.)\n- Handler serializes and returns to client\n\n**Custom storage example**: Custom CRD storage, sharded storage, versioned storage\n\n**Evidence**: `endpoints/installer.go:195-200` - APIInstaller.Install() registers storage\n\n### 5.5 Filter Chain Extension\n\n**Safe extension point**: Add custom filter to beginning of chain\n\n```go\nfunc NewCustomFilter(handler http.Handler) http.Handler {\n    return http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {\n        // Do something before request\n        handler.ServeHTTP(w, r)\n        // Do something after response (if using wrapper)\n    })\n}\n\n// In Config.BuildHandlerChainFunc:\nfunc CustomBuildHandlerChain(apiHandler http.Handler, c *Config) http.Handler {\n    handler := DefaultBuildHandlerChain(apiHandler, c)\n    // Add custom filter on TOP (executed last, wraps all others)\n    handler = NewCustomFilter(handler)\n    return handler\n}\n```\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Ordering**: Filters execute in reverse order of wrapping (outermost wraps all inner filters)\n- **Early termination**: Writing response early (e.g., in custom filter) prevents downstream processing\n- **Context corruption**: Modifying request context incorrectly can break downstream filters\n- **Performance**: Slow filters block all requests\n\n**Safe operations**:\n- Reading request metadata (without modification)\n- Adding to context (idempotent keys only)\n- Recording timing or metrics\n- Logging\n\n**Unsafe operations**:\n- Modifying request path or headers\n- Short-circuiting authentication (must preserve auth contract)\n- Removing critical context values\n\n**Evidence**: `config.go:186` - BuildHandlerChainFunc is called with both handler and config\n\n### 5.6 Post-Start Hooks\n\n**Location**: `server/config.go:153`\n\n```go\ntype PostStartHookConfigEntry struct {\n    Hook PostStartHookFunc\n}\n\ntype PostStartHookFunc func(context.Context, PostStartHookContext) error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Run custom logic after server starts (e.g., initialize custom controllers, download CA certificates)\n\n**Use cases**:\n- Warming up caches\n- Fetching configuration from external source\n- Starting background tasks\n- Initializing custom plugins\n\n**Hooks are executed sequentially**:\n```go\nfor name, entry := range s.PostStartHooks {\n    err := entry.Hook(ctx, postStartHookContext)\n    if err != nil {\n        klog.Fatal(err)  // Server stops on hook failure\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Slow hooks delay readiness**: Server won't pass readiness check until hooks complete\n- **Hook failure stops server**: If hook fails, server terminates\n- **Circular dependencies**: Hooks can depend on other hooks (must get ordering right)\n\n**Evidence**: `server/hooks.go` - hooks implementation\n\n### 5.7 Health Check Extension\n\n**Location**: `server/config.go:199-203`\n\n```go\ntype Config struct {\n    HealthzChecks []healthz.HealthChecker\n    LivezChecks []healthz.HealthChecker\n    ReadyzChecks []healthz.HealthChecker\n}\n```\n\n**Checks**:\n- **Healthz** (`/healthz`): Is server running? Responds 200 OK if any check passes\n- **Livez** (`/livez`): Is server live (not stuck)? All checks must pass\n- **Readyz** (`/readyz`): Is server ready to serve traffic? All checks must pass (stricter than livez)\n\n**Custom check**:\n```go\ntype MyCheck struct{}\n\nfunc (c *MyCheck) Name() string { return \"mycheck\" }\nfunc (c *MyCheck) Check(req *http.Request) error {\n    if !system.IsReady() {\n        return fmt.Errorf(\"system not ready\")\n    }\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Liveness check failure**: Kubernetes will kill pod and restart\n- **Readiness check failure**: Kubernetes removes from load balancer; can cause traffic loss\n- **Slow checks**: Delay Kubernetes detection of problems\n\n**Evidence**: `server/config.go:199-203` - health check configuration\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance Considerations\n\n#### Request Latency Sources\n\n**Measurable latencies** in request path (from `pkg/endpoints/filterlatency/`):\n1. **Authentication** (2-50ms): Token validation, certificate validation\n2. **Authorization** (1-10ms): RBAC rule lookup; webhook can be 50-500ms\n3. **Admission webhooks** (50-500ms): Webhook latency is major contributor\n4. **Storage** (5-50ms): etcd latency; depends on network and etcd load\n5. **Serialization** (1-10ms): Encode/decode, depends on object size\n\n**Latency tracking**: Each filter tracks \"Started\" and \"Completed\" times. These are logged and exported as metrics (`pkg/endpoints/filterlatency/`).\n\n**Optimization strategies**:\n- Cache-friendly admission plugins (local decisions, no webhooks)\n- Fast etcd cluster (SSD, low latency network)\n- Object size limits (reduce serialization overhead)\n- Webhook timeout tuning (balance between strictness and performance)\n\n#### Memory Footprint\n\n**Major sources**:\n1. **In-memory cacher** (default): Caches all list contents in memory (configurable max size)\n2. **Watch buffering**: Each active watch buffers events in memory\n3. **Audit event buffering**: Audit events buffered before written to backend\n4. **Go-restful reflection**: Registers all routes at startup\n\n**Memory optimization**:\n- Reduce cacher size (tradeoff: worse performance)\n- Limit maximum watches per apiserver\n- Batch audit event writes\n- Monitor memory with `go pprof` on debug port\n\n#### Throughput Limits\n\n**Configurable limits**:\n- `MaxRequestsInFlight`: 200 read, 100 write (default)\n- `MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight`: 100 (default)\n- `FlowControl`: Priority and Fairness provides better tuning\n\n**Actual throughput** depends on:\n- Backend (etcd) throughput\n- Admission webhook latency\n- Object size (affects serialization and storage I/O)\n- Network bandwidth\n\n**Evidence**: `config.go:254-259` - in-flight limits\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Failure Recovery\n\n#### High Availability Setup\n\nStandard HA kube-apiserver setup:\n1. **Multiple apiserver instances** (3+): Spread across failure domains\n2. **etcd cluster** (3+): Survives 1 failure; 5 survives 2 failures\n3. **Load balancer** in front: Distributes traffic, removes failed instances\n4. **Health checks**: Load balancer uses `/healthz` to detect failures\n\n#### Graceful Shutdown\n\n**Shutdown sequence** (from `server/graceful_termination.go`):\n\n1. **Stop accepting new requests**: Signal `/readyz` to return failure\n2. **Wait for in-flight requests**: Wait up to `ShutdownTimeout` for requests to complete\n3. **Stop watch streams**: Close all watch connections gracefully\n4. **Shutdown HTTP server**: No more new connections accepted\n5. **Exit**\n\n**Configuration**:\n- `ShutdownTimeout`: Max wait before forcing shutdown (default 15s)\n- `ShutdownDelayDuration`: How long to wait before stopping acceptance (allows LB to remove)\n- `ShutdownWatchTerminationGracePeriod`: Grace period for watch streams\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Shutdown timeout too short**: In-flight requests are abandoned\n- **Shutdown delay too long**: Operator waits a long time for graceful shutdown\n- **Long-running requests**: Webhooks timeout; watch streams hang\n\n**Evidence**: `server/genericapiserver.go:1700+` - shutdown implementation\n\n#### Disaster Recovery\n\n**Data recovery from etcd**:\n- etcd has backup/restore mechanisms\n- `etcdctl snapshot save` → `etcdctl snapshot restore`\n- Kubernetes objects are stored in etcd; recovering etcd recovers cluster\n\n**Evidence**: Not in apiserver code; delegated to etcd\n\n### 6.3 Observability\n\n#### Metrics\n\n**Key metrics** exported by apiserver:\n- `apiserver_request_duration_seconds`: Request latency (histogram)\n- `apiserver_client_certificate_expiration_seconds`: Certificate expiry (useful for alerting)\n- `apiserver_audit_event_total`: Audit event count\n- `apiserver_webhook_duration_seconds`: Webhook latency\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_work_estimated_seats`: Priority/fairness queue depth\n- `etcd_request_duration_seconds`: etcd backend latency\n\n**Prometheus scrape path**: `/metrics` (exposed by GenericAPIServer)\n\n#### Logging\n\n**Request logging** (at debug level):\n```\nklog.V(5).Infof(\"HTTP %s %s\", req.Method, req.URL.Path)\n```\n\n**Filter execution logging** (at very high verbosity):\n```\nklog.V(5).Infof(\"%v %v %q satisfied by gorestful with webservice %v\", name, method, path, service)\n```\n\n**Audit logging** (separate from application logs):\n- Separate file or webhook for audit trail\n- Contains full request/response for compliance and forensics\n- Configurable via audit policy\n\n**Debug socket** (separate from main server):\n- Unprotected `/debug/pprof` endpoint on separate socket\n- Allows profiling without disrupting main API\n\n#### Tracing\n\n**Distributed tracing support** (if enabled via feature gate `APIServerTracing`):\n- Each filter records spans\n- Tracing context propagates through request\n- Integrates with OpenTelemetry\n\n**Filter tracing** (`filters/trace.go`):\n- Each filter has TrackStarted/TrackCompleted\n- Spans are created for each major phase\n\n### 6.4 Capacity Planning\n\n#### CPU Requirements\n\n**CPU usage driven by**:\n- Request throughput (QPS)\n- Admission webhook count/latency\n- Watch stream count\n- Concurrent connections\n\n**Typical**: 0.5-2 cores per apiserver in medium cluster; varies widely\n\n#### Memory Requirements\n\n**Memory usage driven by**:\n- Cacher size (all object cache)\n- Watch buffer sizes\n- Number of active watches\n- Audit event buffering\n\n**Typical**: 512MB-2GB per apiserver; etcd memory overhead separate\n\n#### Network Requirements\n\n**Network usage driven by**:\n- Request/response size\n- Audit log bandwidth\n- etcd replication\n- Watch event bandwidth\n\n#### Storage Requirements\n\n**etcd storage driven by**:\n- Total object count × object size\n- Historical versions (if versioning enabled)\n- Audit log size\n\n**Evidence**: `config.go` contains multiple sizing parameters\n\n### 6.5 Debugging Common Issues\n\n#### High API Latency\n\n**Diagnosis**:\n1. Check filter latency metrics (which filter is slow?)\n2. Check etcd latency\n3. Check webhook latency\n4. Check in-flight request count (if hitting limit)\n\n**Root causes**:\n- Slow etcd cluster (check I/O, network, CPU)\n- Slow admission webhooks (webhook server or network)\n- Overloaded apiserver (too many concurrent requests)\n- Large objects causing slow serialization\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Optimize etcd (add SSDs, reduce etcd load)\n- Fix webhook (optimize logic, add caching)\n- Scale apiserver (add more instances)\n- Reduce object sizes where possible\n\n#### Audit Log Missing Events\n\n**Diagnosis**:\n1. Check audit backend status\n2. Check audit policy rules\n3. Check for audit events in logs\n\n**Root causes**:\n- Audit policy rules don't match request\n- Audit backend unavailable or hung\n- Audit logging disabled\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Review audit policy\n- Check backend (file permissions, webhook connectivity)\n- Enable higher audit level\n\n#### Watch Streams Stuck or Slow\n\n**Diagnosis**:\n1. Check watch connection count\n2. Check cacher buffer size\n3. Check object change rate\n\n**Root causes**:\n- Cacher watch buffer overflowing (client too slow)\n- Network lag between apiserver and client\n- Slow client processing\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Increase cacher buffer (but uses more memory)\n- Use selectors to reduce watch scope\n- Fix client-side processing\n- Scale watchers across multiple clients\n\n---\n\n## 7. Conclusion\n\nThe Kubernetes apiserver library is a sophisticated, modular request handling framework designed for extensibility and reliability. Its architecture separates concerns (authentication, authorization, admission, storage) into pluggable layers connected by explicit request pipelines. Understanding the request flow—from initial HTTP receipt through filter chain, admission control, storage, and back to the client—is essential for extending the system safely.\n\nKey principles for safe customization:\n1. **Understand the flow**: Know where your extension runs in the pipeline\n2. **Preserve contracts**: Don't break assumptions made by downstream components\n3. **Handle failures gracefully**: Slow or crashing extensions can impact the entire system\n4. **Test thoroughly**: Request flows are complex; untested changes cause subtle bugs\n5. **Monitor carefully**: Add metrics and tracing to understand impact\n6. **Document clearly**: Future maintainers need to understand why customizations exist\n\nThe library's thoughtful design—with clear boundaries, explicit filter ordering, and opt-in customization points—makes it a model for extensible infrastructure software.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1151,"cache_read_input_tokens":55864,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1151},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"1d7ccd22-d0d0-4ed0-80a8-47aa0e406421","uuid":"9b124499-9abf-473a-aa37-ff612eef8f06"}
